Now you have nothing at all, and you're not sure how to feel about that.</div> <<display "CleanReturn">> <<endif>>\SCHOOL CURRICULUM The attack on Pearl Harbor in 1941 interrupted a decades-long progressive education movement emphasizing science, engineering, and math, and which focused on critical analysis of American institutions. After Pearl Harbor, when fear and paranoia set in, such progressive notions were scrapped in favor of the "lifestyle adjustment curriculum." This was designed to teach life skills to the 60% of students who would not go on to post-secondary education. About 30% of students would graduate, and there were plenty of jobs available for this level of education. It proposed to teach American students to be good, patriotic (and pliable) citizens, claiming that the old progressive education taught children to be materialistic and gave them bankrupt morals. The "lifestyle" curriculum was criticized (at the time, and also later) for being too soft and non-academic, emphasizing daily life skills (like literacy) over rigorous study (like understanding and questioning what you read). Part of the reason for this focus was a renewed interest in integrating American education with national defense priorities. While recruiting soldiers for World War II, the Army had to reject hundreds of thousands of applicants for being illiterate. They also discovered how disorganized and non-standardized the curriculum could be across various states; the quality of education varied widely. There was also a shortage of people skilled in modern foreign languages. Homework was fairly unknown, especially at lower age levels; most high school students had less than 2 hours per evening. When the Soviets launched Sputnik in 1957 it forced a massive re-think of education in America vis-a-vis national defense priorities, and the burden of nightly homework began to ramp skyward. Courses: reading, grammar, written and mental arithmetic, social studies, science, family life, hygiene, health, religion, speech. Geography (maps), languages, gym, home economics, biology, shop ("industrial arts"). Photography. There would also be an emphasis on geography (especially map familiarity). Biology and home ec courses would start to teach first aid and nursing. During the war, schools would hold drives for paper and scrap metal. Intra-varsity athletics were emphasized, along with calisthenics drills, to increase student health in the event of national need. Social Studies courses focused on problems that related directly to national welfare -- unlike before the war, when the courses focused on critical problems within the US. (Our player in 1948 would have seen both of these techniques.) https://scholarworks.gsu.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1074&context=mse_facpub Sample report card, 10th grade: art, gym, geometry?, study, world history, English, biology Sample report card, 12th grade: art, English, stenography, P.D.?, bookkeeping II, Law, Health-Gym-Study-Gym-Study Sample report card, 10th grade: English II, stenography I, Typing II, Bhp? These experiments were ultimately unsuccessful in preventing polio, but they had an unexpected side effect. The children of those vaccine test subjects were born with a new kind of dimorphic sex chromosome, designated Z or Zeta. The Zeta chromosome can transform its shape and chemical nature from X to Y and back, changing an XX into an XY pair, or vice-versa. It rarely does so when this would result in a non-viable combination, such as YY, although this is mostly because I (the author) don't want to complicate things unnecessarily. Some other author who is better versed in genetics can tackle this variation. What the Zeta chromosome actually _does_ apart from change biological sex is up to the player. The intention is to permit the player to play through each of the scenarios and keep track of the player's decisions. The changes wrought by the Zeta chromosome and the way these affect society depend on what the player chooses. THE CHOICES There are five basic axes along which the player's choices matter. Major decisions from each story are added to the saved calculations, which persist across multiple playthroughs. (The player will have the option to wipe the history and start fresh.) * Sex. Does the Zeta chromosome only affect AFAB or AMAB? If the player always selects "male" to start, then Zeta becomes a condition only of children born and identified as male at birth. The choice of starting character could become constrained to that single sex. If the player chooses a mixture of male and female starting points, the game will allow both AMAB and AFAB characters to be Zetas. * Social. Does society accept or reject these changes? If the player is more open, more forthright, more bold, and more accepting of the changes, society will shift in that direction. Zetas will get more good publicity as role models emerge on early radio and newsreels, and later in the golden age of television. If the player is more secretive or shameful about these changes, and pushes less against the grain, then society will have a less-good view of Zetas; and Zetas of the future are more likely to conceal their natures or face consequences. The world thus becomes the kind of place that the player creates. * Orientation. Does the Zeta chromosome change your orientation or sex drive? If the player chooses to engage in new sexual behaviors (for instance, going from hetero male to hetero female), then at least sometimes the Zeta chromosome makes this happen. If the player chooses to remain with one sexuality (eg, hetero male to lesbian female) then the Zeta chromosome is _not_ known for changing orientation. The game will keep track of how often this happens and make assumptions about later characters' sexuality. * Mental. Does the Zeta chromosome change the way people think? Is the brain itself altered, setting aside matters of orientation? Do Zetas think differently in each state? * Procreation. Since a Zeta always changes during sex, it makes normal methods of proliferation for the Z chromosome impossible. Therefore, one of two methods must be favored. Either the chromosome is _transmissible_ (you can catch Zeta from somewhere), or the chromosome is _lockable_ (your form can be fixed in one state somehow, either temporarily or permanently). All of the above contribute to the kind of world the player creates. If Zetas are looked down upon, and the state is Lockable, then Zetas may try to fix themselves in a favored shape. If Zetas are disfavored and the condition can be caught, then the condition might be inflicted on others out of spite, and transgender people may secretly aspire to catch the condition. And so on.
